class="adr"><span class="postal-code">22301 to 22315, 22320 to 22336</span></td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedrow">\n<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbering_plan" title="Telephone numbering plan">Area code(s)</a></th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Area_code_571" class="mw-redirect" title="Area code 571">571</a>, <a href="/wiki/Area_code_703" class="mw-redirect" title="Area code 703">703</a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedtoprow">\n<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Federal_Information_Processing_Standard" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Information Processing Standard">FIPS code</a></th>\n<td>51-01000<sup id="cite_ref-GR2_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR2-1">[1]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedrow">\n<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_Names_Information_System" title="Geographic Names Information System">GNIS</a> feature ID</th>\n<td>1492456<sup id="cite_ref-GR3_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR3-2">[2]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedtoprow">\n<th scope="row">Website</th>\n<td><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.alexandriava.gov">www<wbr />.alexandriava<wbr />.gov</a></span></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><b>Alexandria</b> is an <a href="/wiki/Independent_city_(United_States)" title="Independent city (United States)">independent city</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._state)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. state)">Commonwealth</a> of <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. As of the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 census</a>, the population was 139,966,<sup id="cite_ref-QF_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QF-3">[3]</a></sup> and in 2016, the population was estimated to be 155,810.<sup id="cite_ref-USCensusEst2015_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USCensusEst2015-4">[4]</a></sup> Located along the western bank of the <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">Potomac River</a>, Alexandria is approximately 7 miles (11&#160;km) south of <a href="/wiki/Downtown,_Washington,_D.C." title="Downtown, Washington, D.C.">downtown Washington, D.C.</a></p>\n<p>Like the rest of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">Northern Virginia</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Central_Maryland" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Maryland">Central Maryland</a>, modern Alexandria has been influenced by its proximity to the U.S. capital. It is largely populated by professionals working in the federal civil service, in the U.S. military, or for one of the many private companies which contract to provide services to the federal government. One of Alexandria\'s largest employers is the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">U.S. Department of Defense</a>. Another is the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Defense_Analyses" title="Institute for Defense Analyses">Institute for Defense Analyses</a>. In 2005, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Patent_and_Trademark_Office" title="United States Patent and Trademark Office">United States Patent and Trademark Office</a> moved to Alexandria.</p>\n<p>The historic center of Alexandria is known as "Old Town". With its concentration of boutiques, restaurants, <a href="/wiki/Antique_shop" title="Antique shop">antique shops</a> and theaters, it is a major draw for all who live in Alexandria as well for visitors. Like Old Town, many Alexandria neighborhoods are compact and walkable. It is the 7th largest and highest-income independent city in Virginia.</p>\n<p>A large portion of adjacent <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">Fairfax County</a> mostly south, but also west of the city is named "Alexandria," but it is under the jurisdiction of Fairfax County and separate from the city; the city is sometimes referred to as the City of Alexandria to avoid confusion (see the "Neighborhoods" paragraph below). In 1920, Virginia\'s General Assembly voted to incorporate what had been Alexandria County as <a href="/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia" title="Arlington County, Virginia">Arlington County</a> to minimize confusion.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span tocsection-20"><a href="#Ecocity"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Ecocity</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Education"><span class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#In_popular_culture"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">In popular culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">14.1</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">14.2</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Alexandria,_Virginia" title="History of Alexandria, Virginia">History of Alexandria, Virginia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Alexandria,_Virginia" title="Timeline of Alexandria, Virginia">Timeline of Alexandria, Virginia</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">Colonial era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Colonial era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1878_Alexandria_County_Virginia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Map labeled &quot;Alexandria County&quot; on old yellowed paper, with Potomac River along upper right" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/1878_Alexandria_County_Virginia.jpg/220px-1878_Alexandria_County_Virginia.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/1878_Alexandria_County_Virginia.jpg/330px-1878_Alexandria_County_Virginia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/1878_Alexandria_County_Virginia.jpg/440px-1878_Alexandria_County_Virginia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7504" data-file-height="4896" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1878_Alexandria_County_Virginia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMap of Alexandria County (1878), including what is now <a href="/wiki/Arlington_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Arlington County">Arlington County</a> and the City of Alexandria. Map includes the names of property owners at that time. City boundaries roughly correspond with Old Town.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On October 21, 1669 a patent granted 6,000 acres (24&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) to Robert Howsing for transporting 120 people to the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia" title="Colony of Virginia">Colony of Virginia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Brockett_and_Rock_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brockett_and_Rock-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:5</sup> That tract would later become the City of Alexandria.<sup id="cite_ref-Brockett_and_Rock_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brockett_and_Rock-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:5</sup> Virginia\'s comprehensive <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_Inspection_Act_of_1730" class="mw-redirect" title="Tobacco Inspection Act of 1730">Tobacco Inspection Law of 1730</a> mandated that all tobacco grown in the colony must be brought to locally designated public warehouses for inspection before sale. One of the sites designated for a warehouse on the upper <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">Potomac River</a> was at the mouth of <a href="/wiki/Hunting_Creek" title="Hunting Creek">Hunting Creek</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> However, the ground proved to be unsuitable, and the warehouse was built half a mile up-river, where the water was deep near the shore.</p>\n<p>Following the 1745 settlement of the Virginia\'s 10 year dispute with Lord Fairfax over the western boundary of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Neck_Proprietary" title="Northern Neck Proprietary">Northern Neck Proprietary</a>, when the Privy Council in London found in favor of Lord Fairfax\'s expanded claim, some of the Fairfax County gentry formed the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Company" title="Ohio Company">Ohio Company</a> of Virginia. They intended to conduct trade into the interior of America, and they required a trading center near the head of navigation on the Potomac. The best location was Hunting Creek tobacco warehouse, since the deep water could easily accommodate sailing ships. Many local tobacco planters, however, wanted a new town further up Hunting Creek, away from nonproductive fields along the river.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Around 1746, Captain <a href="/w/index.php?title=Philip_Alexander_II&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Philip Alexander II (page does not exist)">Philip Alexander II</a> (1704\xe2\x80\x931753) moved to what is south of present Duke Street in Alexandria. His estate, which consisted of 500 acres (2.0&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), was bounded by Hunting Creek, Hooff\'s Run, the Potomac River, and approximately the line which would become Cameron Street. At the opening of Virginia\'s 1748\xe2\x80\x9349 legislative session, there was a petition submitted in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Burgesses" title="House of Burgesses">House of Burgesses</a> on November 1, 1748, that the "inhabitants of Fairfax (Co.) praying that a town may be established at Hunting Creek Warehouse on Potowmack River," as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugh_West&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hugh West (page does not exist)">Hugh West</a> was the owner of the warehouse. The petition was introduced by <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Washington_(1718%E2%80%931752)" title="Lawrence Washington (1718\xe2\x80\x931752)">Lawrence Washington (1718\xe2\x80\x931752)</a>, the representative for Fairfax County and, more importantly, the son-in-law of <a href="/wiki/William_Fairfax" title="William Fairfax">William Fairfax</a> and a founding member of the Ohio Company. To support the company\'s push for a town on the river, Lawrence\'s younger brother <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>, an aspiring surveyor, made a sketch of the shoreline touting the advantages of the tobacco warehouse site.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Since the river site was amidst his estate, Philip opposed the idea and strongly favored a site at the head of Hunting Creek (also known as Great Hunting Creek). It has been said that in order to avoid a predicament the petitioners offered to name the new town <i>Alexandria</i>, in honor of Philip\'s family. As a result, Philip and his cousin Captain <a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Alexander_(captain)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="John Alexander (captain) (page does not exist)">John Alexander</a> (1711\xe2\x80\x931763) gave land to assist in the development of Alexandria, and are thus listed as the founders. This John was the son of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_Alexander_II&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Robert Alexander II (page does not exist)">Robert Alexander II</a> (1688\xe2\x80\x931735). On May 2, 1749, the House of Burgesses approved the river location and ordered "Mr. Washington do go up with a Message to the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Governor%27s_Council" title="Virginia Governor\'s Council">Council</a> and acquaint them that this House have agreed to the Amendments titled An Act for erecting a Town at Hunting Creek Warehouse, in the County of Fairfax."<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> A "Public Vendue" (auction) was advertised for July, and the county surveyor laid out street lanes and town lots. The auction was conducted on July 13\xe2\x80\x9314, 1749.</p>\n<p>Almost immediately upon establishment, the town founders called the new town "Belhaven", believed to be in honor of a Scottish patriot, <a href="/wiki/John_Hamilton,_2nd_Lord_Belhaven_and_Stenton" title="John Hamilton, 2nd Lord Belhaven and Stenton">John Hamilton, 2nd Lord Belhaven and Stenton</a>, the Northern Neck tobacco trade being then dominated by Scots. The name Belhaven was used in official lotteries to raise money for a Church and Market House, but it was never approved by the legislature and fell out of favor in the mid-1750s.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The town of Alexandria did not become incorporated until 1779.</p>\n<p>In 1755, General <a href="/wiki/Edward_Braddock" title="Edward Braddock">Edward Braddock</a> organized his fatal expedition against <a href="/wiki/Fort_Duquesne" title="Fort Duquesne">Fort Duquesne</a> at <a href="/wiki/Carlyle_House" title="Carlyle House">Carlyle House</a> in Alexandria. In April 1755, the governors of Virginia, and the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Maryland" title="Province of Maryland">Maryland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Pennsylvania" title="Province of Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Massachusetts_Bay" title="Province of Massachusetts Bay">Massachusetts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Province_of_New_York" title="Province of New York">New York</a> met to determine upon concerted action against the <a href="/wiki/Early_Modern_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Early Modern France">French</a> in America.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911573_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911573-11">[11]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In March 1785, commissioners from Virginia and Maryland met in Alexandria to discuss the commercial relations of the two states, finishing their business at <a href="/wiki/Mount_Vernon" title="Mount Vernon">Mount Vernon</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Mount_Vernon_Conference" title="Mount Vernon Conference">Mount Vernon Conference</a> concluded on March 28 with an agreement for freedom of trade and freedom of navigation of the Potomac River. The Maryland legislature, in ratifying this agreement on November 22, proposed a conference among representatives from all the states to consider the adoption of definite commercial regulations. This led to the calling of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Annapolis_Convention_of_1786&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Annapolis Convention of 1786 (page does not exist)">Annapolis Convention of 1786</a>, which in turn led to the calling of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Convention_of_1787" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Convention of 1787">Federal Convention of 1787</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911573_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911573-11">[11]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 1791, Alexandria was included in the area chosen by <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> to become the District of Columbia.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_19th_century">Early 19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexandria_Virginia_slave_ship.png" class="image"><img alt="Drawing or etching of quiet river port with many boats and many three-story buildings along water\'s edge" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Alexandria_Virginia_slave_ship.png/220px-Alexandria_Virginia_slave_ship.png" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Alexandria_Virginia_slave_ship.png/330px-Alexandria_Virginia_slave_ship.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Alexandria_Virginia_slave_ship.png/440px-Alexandria_Virginia_slave_ship.png 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="1003" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexandria_Virginia_slave_ship.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nSlave ship taking on slaves at the Alexandria waterfront in 1836. Alexandria\'s slave trade made Virginia a more pro-slavery state after <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia_retrocession#Virginia_retrocession" title="District of Columbia retrocession">retrocession</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In 1814, during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>, a British fleet launched a successful <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_Alexandria" title="Raid on Alexandria">Raid on Alexandria</a>, which surrendered without a fight. As agreed in the terms of surrender the British looted stores and warehouses of mainly flour, <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> In 1823 <a href="/wiki/William_Holland_Wilmer" title="William Holland Wilmer">William Holland Wilmer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Scott_Key" title="Francis Scott Key">Francis Scott Key</a>, and others founded the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Theological_Seminary" title="Virginia Theological Seminary">Virginia Theological Seminary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:116</sup> From 1828 to 1836,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Alexandria was home to the <a href="/wiki/Franklin_%26_Armfield" class="mw-redirect" title="Franklin &amp; Armfield">Franklin &amp; Armfield</a> Slave Market, one of the largest slave trading companies in the country. By the 1830s, they were sending more than 1,000 slaves annually from Alexandria to their <a href="/wiki/Natchez,_Mississippi" title="Natchez, Mississippi">Natchez, Mississippi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a> markets to help meet the demand for slaves in Mississippi and surrounding states.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Later owned by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Price,_Birch_%26_Co.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Price, Birch &amp; Co. (page does not exist)">Price, Birch &amp; Co.</a>, the slave pen became a jail under <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">Union</a> occupation.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>\n<p>A portion of the City of Alexandria\xe2\x80\x94most of the area now known as "Old Town" as well as <a href="/wiki/Boundary_Markers_of_the_Original_District_of_Columbia" title="Boundary Markers of the Original District of Columbia">the areas of the city northeast of what is now King Street</a>\xe2\x80\x94and all of today\'s <a href="/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia" title="Arlington County, Virginia">Arlington County</a> share the distinction of having been originally in Virginia, ceded to the U.S. Government to form the <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">District of Columbia</a>, and later <a href="/wiki/Retrocession_(District_of_Columbia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Retrocession (District of Columbia)">retroceded to Virginia</a> by the federal government in 1846, when the District was reduced in size to exclude the portion south of the Potomac River. Over time, a movement grew to separate Alexandria from the District of Columbia (the <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia_retrocession" title="District of Columbia retrocession">District of Columbia retrocession</a>). As competition grew with the port of <a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_Washington,_D.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Georgetown, Washington, D.C.">Georgetown</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_and_Ohio_Canal" title="Chesapeake and Ohio Canal">Chesapeake and Ohio Canal</a> fostered development on the north side of the Potomac River, the city\'s economy stagnated, together with the loss of representation and rights to vote and failed expectations for economic benefit from the new district. Alexandria was also an important port and market in the <a href="/wiki/Slave_trade" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a>, and there were increasing talk of <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_States" title="Abolitionism in the United States">abolition</a> of slavery in the national capital. Alexandria\'s economy would suffer greatly if slavery were outlawed. After a referendum, voters petitioned Congress and Virginia to return the area to Virginia. Congress retroceded the area to Virginia on July 9, 1846.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The City of Alexandria was re-chartered in 1852 and became independent of <a href="/wiki/Alexandria_County,_D.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Alexandria County, D.C.">Alexandria County</a> in 1870. The remaining portion of Alexandria County changed its name to <a href="/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia" title="Arlington County, Virginia">Arlington County</a> in 1920.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_19th_century">Late 19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Late 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fort-lyon-alexandria-virginia-vhs00032-1-.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Hand-drawn map of part of Virginia with Potomac river on right. It shows railroads and Civil War forts." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Fort-lyon-alexandria-virginia-vhs00032-1-.jpg/170px-Fort-lyon-alexandria-virginia-vhs00032-1-.jpg" width="170" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Fort-lyon-alexandria-virginia-vhs00032-1-.jpg/255px-Fort-lyon-alexandria-virginia-vhs00032-1-.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Fort-lyon-alexandria-virginia-vhs00032-1-.jpg/340px-Fort-lyon-alexandria-virginia-vhs00032-1-.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1609" data-file-height="2158" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fort-lyon-alexandria-virginia-vhs00032-1-.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMap of Alexandria showing the forts that were constructed to defend Washington during the Civil War</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexandria_Bird%27s_Eye_View_1863.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Elegant drawing of city from above Potomac river looking west over streets of Alexandria and several sailing boats in foreground" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Alexandria_Bird%27s_Eye_View_1863.jpg/220px-Alexandria_Bird%27s_Eye_View_1863.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Alexandria_Bird%27s_Eye_View_1863.jpg/330px-Alexandria_Bird%27s_Eye_View_1863.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Alexandria_Bird%27s_Eye_View_1863.jpg/440px-Alexandria_Bird%27s_Eye_View_1863.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7624" data-file-height="5112" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexandria_Bird%27s_Eye_View_1863.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA bird\'s eye view of Alexandria from the Potomac in 1863. <a href="/wiki/Fort_Ellsworth" title="Fort Ellsworth">Fort Ellsworth</a> is visible on the hill in the center background.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The first fatalities of the North and South in the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> occurred in Alexandria. Within a month of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Sumter" title="Battle of Fort Sumter">Battle of Fort Sumter</a>, where two died, Union troops occupied Alexandria, landing troops at the base of King Street on the Potomac River on May 24, 1861. A few blocks up King Street from their landing site, the commander of the <a href="/wiki/11th_New_York_Volunteer_Infantry_Regiment" class="mw-redirect" title="11th New York Volunteer Infantry Regiment">New York Fire Zouaves</a>, Colonel <a href="/wiki/Elmer_E._Ellsworth" title="Elmer E. Ellsworth">Elmer E. Ellsworth</a>, sortied with a small detachment to retrieve a large <a href="/wiki/Confederate_flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Confederate flag">Confederate flag</a> displayed on the roof of the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_House_(Alexandria,_Virginia)" title="Marshall House (Alexandria, Virginia)">Marshall House Inn</a> that had been visible from the White House. While descending from the roof, Ellsworth was shot dead by Captain James W. Jackson, the hotel\'s proprietor. One of the Ellsworth\'s soldier immediately killed Jackson.<sup id="cite_ref-sonofthesouth.net_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sonofthesouth.net-18">[18]</a></sup> Ellsworth was publicized as a Union martyr, and the incident generated great excitement in the North, with many children being named for him.<sup id="cite_ref-sonofthesouth.net_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sonofthesouth.net-18">[18]</a></sup> Jackson\'s death defending his home caused a similar, though less lasting sensation, in the South.</p>\n<p>Alexandria remained under military occupation until the end of the war. <a href="/wiki/Fort_Ward_(Virginia)" title="Fort Ward (Virginia)">Fort Ward</a>, one of a ring of forts built by the Union army for the defense of <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, is located inside the boundaries of present-day Alexandria.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> After the creation by Washington of the state of <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a> in 1863 and until the close of the war, Alexandria was the seat of the so-called <a href="/wiki/Restored_Government_of_Virginia" title="Restored Government of Virginia">Restored Government of Virginia</a>, also known as the "Alexandria Government".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911573_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911573-11">[11]</a></sup> During the Union occupation, a recurring contention between the Alexandria citizenry and the military occupiers was the Union army\'s periodic insistence that church services include prayers for the President of the United States. Failure to do so resulted in incidents including the arrest of ministers in their church.</p>\n<p>Escaped <a href="/wiki/African_American" class="mw-redirect" title="African American">African American</a> slaves poured into Alexandria. Safely behind Union lines, the cities of Alexandria and Washington offered comparative freedom and employment. Alexandria became a major supply depot and transport and hospital center for the Union army.<sup id="cite_ref-Office_of_Historic_Alexandria_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office_of_Historic_Alexandria-20">[20]</a></sup> Until the <a href="/wiki/Emancipation_Proclamation" title="Emancipation Proclamation">Emancipation Proclamation</a>, escaped slaves legally remained the property of their owners. Therefore, they were labeled <a href="/wiki/Contraband_(American_Civil_War)" title="Contraband (American Civil War)">contrabands</a> to avoid returning them to their masters. Contrabands worked the Union army in various support roles. By the fall of 1863, the population of Alexandria had exploded to 18,000\xe2\x80\x94an increase of 10,000 people in 16 months.<sup id="cite_ref-Office_of_Historic_Alexandria_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office_of_Historic_Alexandria-20">[20]</a></sup></p>\n<p>As of ratification of <a href="/wiki/Fifteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fifteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">the Fifteenth Amendment</a>, Alexandria County\'s black population was more than 8,700, or about half the total number of residents in the county. This newly enfranchised constituency provided the support necessary to elect the first black Alexandrians to the City Council and the Virginia Legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-alexandriaweba.com_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alexandriaweba.com-21">[21]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_few_of_the_young_boys_working_on_the_night_shift_at_the_glass_factory._Alexandria,_Va._-_NARA_-_523440.jpg" class="image"><img alt="20-25 males facing camera in a row, mostly children. Ages vary. They are in work clothes. Some are dirty. Some wear caps. They stand on dirt with a wooden building behind them." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/A_few_of_the_young_boys_working_on_the_night_shift_at_the_glass_factory._Alexandria%2C_Va._-_NARA_-_523440.jpg/220px-A_few_of_the_young_boys_working_on_the_night_shift_at_the_glass_factory._Alexandria%2C_Va._-_NARA_-_523440.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/A_few_of_the_young_boys_working_on_the_night_shift_at_the_glass_factory._Alexandria%2C_Va._-_NARA_-_523440.jpg/330px-A_few_of_the_young_boys_working_on_the_night_shift_at_the_glass_factory._Alexandria%2C_Va._-_NARA_-_523440.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/A_few_of_the_young_boys_working_on_the_night_shift_at_the_glass_factory._Alexandria%2C_Va._-_NARA_-_523440.jpg/440px-A_few_of_the_young_boys_working_on_the_night_shift_at_the_glass_factory._Alexandria%2C_Va._-_NARA_-_523440.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2150" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_few_of_the_young_boys_working_on_the_night_shift_at_the_glass_factory._Alexandria,_Va._-_NARA_-_523440.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nChild laborers working at a glass factory in Alexandria, 1911. Photo by <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Hine" title="Lewis Hine">Lewis Hine</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Confederate_Memorial_in_Alexandria,_Virginia_(3359940265).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/The_Confederate_Memorial_in_Alexandria%2C_Virginia_%283359940265%29.jpg/220px-The_Confederate_Memorial_in_Alexandria%2C_Virginia_%283359940265%29.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/The_Confederate_Memorial_in_Alexandria%2C_Virginia_%283359940265%29.jpg/330px-The_Confederate_Memorial_in_Alexandria%2C_Virginia_%283359940265%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/The_Confederate_Memorial_in_Alexandria%2C_Virginia_%283359940265%29.jpg/440px-The_Confederate_Memorial_in_Alexandria%2C_Virginia_%283359940265%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="536" data-file-height="350" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Confederate_Memorial_in_Alexandria,_Virginia_(3359940265).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nConfederate Memorial on <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_Memorial_Parkway" title="George Washington Memorial Parkway">George Washington Memorial Parkway</a> (circa 1920)</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>At the turn of the 20th century the most common production in the city was glass, fertilizer, beer and leather. The glass often went into beer bottles. Much of the Virginia Glass Company effort went to supply the demands of the Robert Portner Brewing Company, until fire destroyed the St. Asaph Street plant on February 18, 1905. The Old Dominion Glass Company also had a glass works fall to fire, then built a new one. The Belle Pre Bottle Company held a monopoly on a milk bottle that they patented, yet that organization only lasted 10 years.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Most businesses were smaller where the business occupied the first floor of a building and the owner and family lived above. <sup id="cite_ref-Illustrated_History_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Illustrated_History-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:50</sup> Prohibition closed Portner Brewing in 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-Illustrated_History_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Illustrated_History-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:50</sup></p>\n<p>President <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a> visited the Virginia Shipbuilding Corporation on May 30, 1918 to drive the first rivet into the keel of the <a href="/wiki/USS_Gunston_Hall" title="USS Gunston Hall">USS Gunston Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Illustrated_History_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Illustrated_History-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:50</sup> In 1930 Alexandria annexed the town adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Potomac_Yard" title="Potomac Yard">Potomac Yard</a> incorporated in 1908 named <a href="/wiki/Potomac,_Virginia" title="Potomac, Virginia">Potomac</a>. In 1938 the Mt. Vernon Drive-In cinema opened.<sup id="cite_ref-cinema_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cinema-24">[24]</a></sup> In 1939 the segregated public library experienced a <a href="/wiki/Sit-in" title="Sit-in">sit-in</a> organized by <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Wilbert_Tucker" title="Samuel Wilbert Tucker">Samuel Wilbert Tucker</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In 1940 both the Robert Robinson Library, which is now the Alexandria Black History Museum, and the Vernon Theatre opened<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jim_Morrison" title="Jim Morrison">Jim Morrison</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Doors" title="The Doors">The Doors</a></i>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Cass_Elliot" title="Cass Elliot">Cass Elliot</a> and John Phillips of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mamas_%26_The_Papas" class="mw-redirect" title="The Mamas &amp; The Papas">The Mamas &amp; The Papas</a></i> attended the George Washington High School in the 1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-visitalexandriava_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitalexandriava-27">[27]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 1955 the <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Fords</a> moved to Alexandria from <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Georgetown (Washington, D.C.)">Georgetown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:95</sup> In March 1959 Lieutenant Colonel William Henry Whalen, the "highest-ranking American ever recruited as a mole by the Russian Intelligence Service," provided Colonel Sergei A. Edemski three <a href="/wiki/Classified_information" title="Classified information">classified</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">Army</a> manuals in exchange for $3,500 at a shopping center parking lot within the city.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Agents of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">Federal Bureau of Investigation</a> later arrested Whalen on July 12, 1966 at his home in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:p1</sup> In 1961 the <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson_Bridge" title="Woodrow Wilson Bridge">Woodrow Wilson Bridge</a> opened.<sup id="cite_ref-20th-Timeline_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20th-Timeline-31">[31]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 1965 the city integrated schools.<sup id="cite_ref-Remember_the_Titans._Sort_Of_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Remember_the_Titans._Sort_Of-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:69</sup> In 1971 the city consolidated all high school students into <a href="/wiki/T._C._Williams_High_School" title="T. C. Williams High School">T. C. Williams High School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Remember_the_Titans._Sort_Of_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Remember_the_Titans._Sort_Of-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:69</sup> The same year that head coach <a href="/wiki/Herman_Boone" title="Herman Boone">Herman Boone</a> joined the school and lead the football team to at 13-0 season, state championship, and national championship runner-up; the basis for the 2000 film <i><a href="/wiki/Remember_the_Titans" title="Remember the Titans">Remember the Titans</a></i> were Boone was portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Denzel_Washington" title="Denzel Washington">Denzel Washington</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> In 1972 Clifford T. Cline purchased the 1890 <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">Victorian</a> house at 219 King Street and converted it into the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Creole_cuisine" title="Louisiana Creole cuisine">Creole</a> serving Two-Nineteen Restaurant.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:167</sup> In 1973 Nora Lamborne and Beverly Beidler became the first women elected to the city council.<sup id="cite_ref-Illustrated_History_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Illustrated_History-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:63</sup> In 1974 the <a href="/wiki/Torpedo_Factory_Art_Center" title="Torpedo Factory Art Center">Torpedo Factory Art Center</a> opened.<sup id="cite_ref-visitalexandriava_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitalexandriava-27">[27]</a></sup> In 1983 the <a href="/wiki/King_Street%E2%80%93Old_Town_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="King Street\xe2\x80\x93Old Town Station">King Street\xe2\x80\x93Old Town Station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eisenhower_Avenue_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Eisenhower Avenue Station">Eisenhower Avenue Station</a> both opened.<sup id="cite_ref-20th-Timeline_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20th-Timeline-31">[31]</a></sup> In 1984 the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Saudi_Academy" title="Islamic Saudi Academy">Islamic Saudi Academy</a> opened.<sup id="cite_ref-pluralism_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pluralism-35">[35]</a></sup> and Parker-Gray historic district<sup id="cite_ref-visitalexandriava_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitalexandriava-27">[27]</a></sup> In 1991 Patricia Ticer became the first women elected mayor.<sup id="cite_ref-Illustrated_History_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Illustrated_History-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:63</sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_libraries">History of libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History of libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>John Wise, a local Alexandria businessman and hotel keeper, hosted a meeting in his home in 1789 to discuss the creation of a Society for the Promotion of Useful Knowledge. Members include Rev. James Muir, physician <a href="/wiki/Elisha_Cullen_Dick" class="mw-redirect" title="Elisha Cullen Dick">Elisha Cullen Dick</a>, and George Washington\'s personal attorney <a href="/wiki/Charles_Lee_(Attorney_General)" title="Charles Lee (Attorney General)">Charles Lee</a>. The Society did not last for long. However, on July 24, 1794, the founders of the Society once again met at Wise\'s home to establish a subscription library. During the first year, one hundred nineteen men joined the circulating library which was to be called the Library Company of Alexandria. Members agreed to pay an initiation fee and annual dues. The company was chartered as a corporation in 1798 in an act passed by the <a href="/wiki/General_Assembly_of_Virginia" class="mw-redirect" title="General Assembly of Virginia">General Assembly of Virginia</a>.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stabler-Leadbeater_Apothecary_Shop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Stabler-Leadbeater_Apothecary_Shop.jpg/170px-Stabler-Leadbeater_Apothecary_Shop.jpg" width="170" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Stabler-Leadbeater_Apothecary_Shop.jpg/255px-Stabler-Leadbeater_Apothecary_Shop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Stabler-Leadbeater_Apothecary_Shop.jpg/340px-Stabler-Leadbeater_Apothecary_Shop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="739" data-file-height="1024" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stabler-Leadbeater_Apothecary_Shop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nFirst city library location within an apothecary shop</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Druggist Edward Stabler was elected the first librarian and the library\'s first location is believed to have been housed in his <a href="/wiki/Stabler-Leadbeater_Apothecary_Shop" title="Stabler-Leadbeater Apothecary Shop">apothecary shop</a>. James Kennedy was elected the second librarian, and the library moved to his residence and place of business. Kennedy sold books from his personal collection to the Library Company. Those books and other bought from two local merchants formed the foundation of the subscription library. The first catalog of the library\'s collection was published in 1797. The collection grew over time, bolstered in part by the fact that some members paid their dues in books. Most members were initially men, although records exist showing some women were members as early as 1798. One noted female member in 1817 was <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lee_Fitzhugh_Custis" title="Mary Lee Fitzhugh Custis">Mary L.F. Custis</a>, wife of <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_Parke_Custis" title="George Washington Parke Custis">George Washington Parke Custis</a>.</p>\n<p>The catalog published in 1801 indicated a collection of 452 books, mostly on history and travel. By 1815, there were 1,022 entries in the catalog, and the collection had added more biographies, fiction, and magazines. The library was housed in several locations over the ensuing years, including the New Market House next to the City Hall, the <a href="/wiki/Lyceum" title="Lyceum">Lyceum</a> Company building, and Peabody Hall, which was owned by the Alexandria School Board. Raising funds for the library was a continuing challenge. In 1853, a lecture series was created to raise money. Speakers included Professor <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Henry" title="Joseph Henry">Joseph Henry</a> of the Smithsonian, Colonel <a href="/wiki/Francis_H._Smith" class="mw-redirect" title="Francis H. Smith">Francis H. Smith</a> of the Virginia Military Institute, and humorist <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bagby" class="mw-redirect" title="George W. Bagby">George W. Bagby</a>.</p>\n<p>The arrival of the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a> in 1861 took its toll on the library collection. Members were able to remove some of the collection prior to the library\'s occupation by Union troops. The library was used as a hospital and much of the library\'s collection was lost during this time. After the war, the building was sold to a private owner who planned to turn the building into a private residence and asked the library to remove what was left of the collection. Funds continued to be hard to come by and in 1879, the Library Company closed. The remainder of its collection was stored in Peabody Hall.</p>\n<p>In 1897, a group of women in Alexandria formed the Alexandria Library Association. The leaders of the group were Virginia Corse, Mrs. William B. Smoot, and Virginia Burke. They petitioned the school board to open a subscription library in Peabody Hall, using the old books stored there. Permission was given and doors to the new subscription library opened on December 1, 1897. In 1902, the library moved to the first floor of a house in the 1300 block of Prince Street while negotiations were underway for a permanent move to the Confederate Hall, located at 806 Prince Street. In May 1903, the library moved to the Confederate Hall, now known as the Robert E. Lee Camp Hall Museum, where it stayed for 34 years.</p>\n<p>In 1936, Dr. and Mrs. Robert South Barrett presented a proposal to the Library Association. They agreed to donate a building in memory of Dr. Barrett\'s mother, <a href="/wiki/Kate_Waller_Barrett" title="Kate Waller Barrett">Kate Waller Barrett</a>, if the city would commit to running it as a public library. The city agreed and the Society of Friends offered a 99-year lease on an old Quaker graveyard located on Queen Street. The old library was closed on March 1 for the books to be packed and moved to the new library, which opened to the public in August 1937. The Alexandria Library Association became the Alexandria Library Society.</p>\n<p>In 1939, the Barrett library was the scene of possibly the nation\'s first sit-in demonstrations, as Samuel Tucker, a young law school graduate from the neighborhood, and several other African-American residents insisted on access to the racially segregated library where they had been banned. Tucker later became a prominent attorney in Richmond.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 1947, the Library Society was reconstituted and took the earlier historic name Alexandria Library Company. A lecture series was also revived. Speakers included <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a> biographer <a href="/wiki/Dumas_Malone" title="Dumas Malone">Dumas Malone</a>. Some of the books belonging in the original collection of the Alexandria Library Company can now be found in the Local History/Special Collections Room at the Queen Street library that still carries Mrs. Barrett\'s name.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 1948, <a href="/wiki/Ellen_Coolidge_Burke" title="Ellen Coolidge Burke">Ellen Coolidge Burke</a> became director. Burke brought <a href="/wiki/Bookmobile" title="Bookmobile">bookmobile</a> services to Alexandria, one of the first services in Virginia. She oversaw the growth of the library system by the addition of two new branch libraries. In April 1968 the Ellen Coolidge Burke Branch at 4701 Seminary Road was opened, and in December 1969 the <a href="/w/index.php?title=James_M._Duncan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="James M. Duncan (page does not exist)">James M. Duncan</a> branch at 2501 Commonwealth Avenue. Burke retired in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div style="width:400px;float:right;clear:right">\n<div style="width:400px;padding:0">\n<div style="position:relative;width:400px"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexandria,_Virginia_surrounding_area.svg" class="image" title="Alexandria, Virginia is located in Alexandria area"><img alt="Alexandria, Virginia is located in Alexandria area" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Alexandria%2C_Virginia_surrounding_area.svg/400px-Alexandria%2C_Virginia_surrounding_area.svg.png" width="400" height="247" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Alexandria%2C_Virginia_surrounding_area.svg/600px-Alexandria%2C_Virginia_surrounding_area.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Alexandria%2C_Virginia_surrounding_area.svg/800px-Alexandria%2C_Virginia_surrounding_area.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="875" data-file-height="541" /></a>\n<div style="position:absolute;top:99.831%;left:47.539%">\n<div style="position:absolute;left:-0px;top:-0px;line-height:0"></div>\n<div style="font-size:100%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;left:1px;text-align:left"><span style="padding:1px;float:left"><a href="/wiki/Charles_County,_Maryland" title="Charles County, Maryland">Charles</a></span></div>\n</div>\n<div style="position:absolute;top:48.935%;left:98.145%">\n<div style="position:absolute;left:-0px;top:-0px;line-height:0"></div>\n<div style="font-size:100%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;right:1px;text-align:right"><span style="padding:1px;float:right"><a href="/wiki/Prince_George%27s_County,_Maryland" title="Prince George\'s County, Maryland">Prince&#160;George\'s</a></span></div>\n</div>\n<div style="position:absolute;top:59.307%;left:59.034%">\n<div style="position:absolute;left:-0px;top:-0px;line-height:0"></div>\n<div style="font-size:100%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:1px;left:-3em;text-align:center"><span style="padding:1px"><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Alexandria</a></span></div>\n</div>\n<div style="position:absolute;top:29.685%;left:40.027%">\n<div style="position:absolute;left:-0px;top:-0px;line-height:0"></div>\n<div style="font-size:100%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:1px;left:-3em;text-align:center"><span style="padding:1px"><a href="/wiki/Arlington,_Virginia" class="mw-redirect" title="Arlington, Virginia">Arlington</a></span></div>\n</div>\n<div style="position:absolute;top:77.656%;left:31.416%">\n<div style="position:absolute;left:-0px;top:-0px;line-height:0"></div>\n<div style="font-size:100%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;left:1px;text-align:left"><span style="padding:1px;float:left"><a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">Fairfax&#160;County</a></span></div>\n</div>\n<div style="position:absolute;top:27.509%;left:17.7%">\n<div style="position:absolute;left:-0px;top:-0px;line-height:0"></div>\n<div style="font-size:100%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;bottom:1px;left:-3em;text-align:center"><span style="padding:1px"><a href="/wiki/Falls_Church,_Virginia" title="Falls Church, Virginia">Falls Church</a></span></div>\n</div>\n<div style="position:absolute;top:0.521%;left:69.322%">\n<div style="position:absolute;left:-0px;top:-0px;line-height:0"></div>\n<div style="font-size:100%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:1px;left:-3em;text-align:center"><span style="padding:1px"><a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington</a></span></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a>, the city has a total area of 15.5 square miles (40.1&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), of which 15.0 square miles (38.9&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) is land and 0.42 square miles (1.1&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), or 2.85%, is water.<sup id="cite_ref-GR1_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR1-40">[40]</a></sup> Alexandria is bounded on the east by the <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">Potomac River</a>, on the north and northwest by <a href="/wiki/Arlington_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Arlington County">Arlington County</a>, and on the south by <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">Fairfax County</a>. The western portions of the city were annexed from those two entities beginning in the 1930s.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Address_(geography)" title="Address (geography)">addressing system</a> in Alexandria is not uniform and reflects the consolidation of several originally separate communities into a single city. In Old Town Alexandria, building numbers are assigned north and south from <a href="/wiki/King_Street_(Alexandria,_Virginia)" title="King Street (Alexandria, Virginia)">King Street</a> and west (only) from the Potomac River. In the areas formerly in the town of <a href="/wiki/Potomac,_Virginia" title="Potomac, Virginia">Potomac</a>, such as Del Ray and St. Elmo, building numbers are assigned east and west from Commonwealth Avenue and north (only) from King Street. In the western parts of the city, building numbers are assigned north and south from <a href="/wiki/Virginia_State_Route_236" title="Virginia State Route 236">Duke Street</a>.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/ZIP_code" class="mw-redirect" title="ZIP code">ZIP code</a> prefix 223 uniquely identifies the Alexandria postal area.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> However, the Alexandria postal area extends into <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">Fairfax County</a> and includes addresses outside of the city. Delivery areas have ZIP codes 22301, 22302, 22203, 22304, 22305, 22306, 22307, 22308, 22309, 22310, 22311, 22312, 22314, and 22315, with other ZIP codes in use for <a href="/wiki/Post_office_box" class="mw-redirect" title="Post office box">post office boxes</a> and large mailers (22313, 22331, 22332, 22333).</p>\n<p>Part of the <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_Memorial_Parkway" title="George Washington Memorial Parkway">George Washington Memorial Parkway</a> is the one national protected area within the borders of Alexandria.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjacent_jurisdictions">Adjacent jurisdictions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Adjacent jurisdictions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 20em; -webkit-column-width: 20em; column-width: 20em;">\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia" title="Arlington County, Virginia">Arlington County, Virginia</a> \xe2\x80\x93 north</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_County,_Maryland" title="Charles County, Maryland">Charles County, Maryland</a> \xe2\x80\x93 southeast</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia" class="mw-redirect" title="District of Columbia">District of Columbia</a> \xe2\x80\x93 northeast</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">Fairfax County, Virginia</a> \xe2\x80\x93 west and south</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Prince_George%27s_County,_Maryland" title="Prince George\'s County, Maryland">Prince George\'s County, Maryland</a> \xe2\x80\x93 east</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neighborhoods">Neighborhoods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Neighborhoods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_neighborhoods_in_Alexandria,_Virginia" title="List of neighborhoods in Alexandria, Virginia">List of neighborhoods in Alexandria, Virginia</a></div>\n<p>Neighborhoods in Alexandria include Old Town, Eisenhower Valley, Rosemont, The Berg, Parker-Gray, Del Ray, Arlandria, West End, North Ridge, and Potomac Yard. Many areas outside the city have an Alexandria mailing address yet are a part of <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">Fairfax County</a> including: <a href="/wiki/Hollin_Hills" title="Hollin Hills">Hollin Hills</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franconia,_Virginia" title="Franconia, Virginia">Franconia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Groveton,_Virginia" title="Groveton, Virginia">Groveton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hybla_Valley,_Virginia" title="Hybla Valley, Virginia">Hybla Valley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huntington,_Virginia" title="Huntington, Virginia">Huntington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belle_Haven,_Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Belle Haven, Fairfax County, Virginia">Belle Haven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Vernon,_Virginia" title="Mount Vernon, Virginia">Mount Vernon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Hunt,_Virginia" title="Fort Hunt, Virginia">Fort Hunt</a>, Engleside, Burgundy Village, Waynewood, Wilton Woods, <a href="/wiki/Rose_Hill,_Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Rose Hill, Fairfax County, Virginia">Rose Hill</a>, Virginia Hills, Hayfield, and <a href="/wiki/Kingstowne,_Virginia" title="Kingstowne, Virginia">Kingstowne</a>. Some refer to these areas as Lower Alexandria, South Alexandria, or Alexandria, Fairfax County.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The climate in this area is characterized by hot, humid summers and generally mild to cool winters. According to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Classification" class="mw-redirect" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen Climate Classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen Climate Classification</a> system, Alexandria has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a>, abbreviated "Cfa" on climate maps.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="toccolours" style="border-spacing: 1px; text-align: center;">33.7%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center"><b><a href="/wiki/1940_United_States_Census" title="1940 United States Census">1940</a></b></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px;">33,523</td>\n<td style="font-size:85%"></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">38.8%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center"><b><a href="/wiki/1950_United_States_Census" title="1950 United States Census">1950</a></b></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px;">61,787</td>\n<td style="font-size:85%"></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">84.3%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center"><b><a href="/wiki/1960_United_States_Census" title="1960 United States Census">1960</a></b></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px;">91,023</td>\n<td style="font-size:85%"></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">47.3%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center"><b><a href="/wiki/1970_United_States_Census" title="1970 United States Census">1970</a></b></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px;">110,927</td>\n<td style="font-size:85%"></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">21.9%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center"><b><a href="/wiki/1980_United_States_Census" title="1980 United States Census">1980</a></b></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px;">103,217</td>\n<td style="font-size:85%"></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">\xe2\x88\x927.0%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center"><b><a href="/wiki/1990_United_States_Census" title="1990 United States Census">1990</a></b></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px;">111,183</td>\n<td style="font-size:85%"></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">7.7%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center"><b><a href="/wiki/2000_United_States_Census" title="2000 United States Census">2000</a></b></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px;">128,283</td>\n<td style="font-size:85%"></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">15.4%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center"><b><a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010</a></b></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px;">139,966</td>\n<td style="font-size:85%"></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">9.1%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center"><b>Est. 2016</b></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px;">155,810</td>\n<td style="font-size:85%"><sup id="cite_ref-USCensusEst2016_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USCensusEst2016-43">[43]</a></sup></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">11.3%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="4" style="border-top:1px solid black; font-size:85%; text-align:center">U.S. Decennial Census<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><br />\n1790\xe2\x80\x931960<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> 1900\xe2\x80\x931990<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><br />\n1990\xe2\x80\x932000<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>At the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-GR8_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR8-48">[48]</a></sup> there were 139,966 people, 68,082 households and 30,978 families residing in the city. The <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> was 8,452.0 per square mile (3,262.9/km\xc2\xb2). There were 68,082 housing units at an average density of 4,233.2 per square mile (1,634.2/km\xc2\xb2). The folks of the city were:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>60.9% <a href="/wiki/White_American" class="mw-redirect" title="White American">White</a></li>\n<li>21.8% <a href="/wiki/Black_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Black American">African American</a></li>\n<li>6.0% <a href="/wiki/Asian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian American">Asian</a> (1.3% Indian, 1.0% Filipino, 0.9% Chinese, 0.8% Korean, 0.5% Thai, 0.3% Vietnamese, 0.2% Japanese, 1.0% Other)</li>\n<li>0.4% <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native American</a></li>\n<li>0.1% <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Islander American">Pacific Islander</a></li>\n<li>3.7% from two or more races</li>\n<li>16.1% of the population were <a href="/wiki/Hispanics_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Hispanics in the United States">Hispanics or Latinos</a> of any national origin (4.6% Salvadoran, 1.7% Mexican, 1.6% Honduran, 1.1% Guatemalan, 1.1% Puerto Rican, 0.9% Bolivian, 0.8% Peruvian, 0.4% Colombian)</li>\n</ul>\n<p>In 2000, there were 61,889 households of which 18.6% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 32.2% were <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">married couples</a> living together, 9.2% had a female householder with no husband present, and 55.2% were non-families. 43.4% of all households were made up of individuals and 6.8% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.04 and the average family size was 2.87.</p>\n<p>The age distribution was 16.8% under the age of 18, 9.2% from 18 to 24, 43.5% from 25 to 44, 21.5% from 45 to 64, and 9.0% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 34 years. For every 100 females there were 93.5 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 91.7 males.</p>\n<p>According to a 2007 estimate, the <a href="/wiki/Median_household_income" class="mw-redirect" title="Median household income">median household income</a> was $80,806 and the median family income was $102,435.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Males had a median income of $47,514 versus $41,254 for females. The <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> for the city was $37,645. 8.9% of the population and 6.8% of families were below the <a href="/wiki/Poverty_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Poverty line">poverty line</a>. 13.9% of those under the age of 18 and 9.0% of those 65 and older were living below the poverty line.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit Analyses">Institute for Defense Analyses</a>, <a href="/wiki/VSE_Corporation" title="VSE Corporation">VSE</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pentagon_Federal_Credit_Union" title="Pentagon Federal Credit Union">Pentagon Federal Credit Union</a>.</p>\n<p>Alexandria is home to numerous <a href="/wiki/Trade_group" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade group">trade associations</a>, charities, and non-profit organizations including the national headquarters of groups such as the <a href="/wiki/American_Diabetes_Association" title="American Diabetes Association">American Diabetes Association</a>, <a href="/wiki/BoatUS" title="BoatUS">BoatUS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Charities,_USA" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic Charities, USA">Catholic Charities</a>, <a title="Good360">Good360</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Relief_USA" title="Islamic Relief USA">Islamic Relief USA</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Way_of_America" title="United Way of America">United Way</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volunteers_of_America" title="Volunteers of America">Volunteers of America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Salvation_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Salvation Army">Salvation Army</a>. Other organizations located in Alexandria include <a href="/wiki/American_Coalition_for_Clean_Coal_Electricity" title="American Coalition for Clean Coal Electricity">American Coalition for Clean Coal Electricity</a>, the <a href="/wiki/American_Counseling_Association" title="American Counseling Association">American Counseling Association</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Centre_for_Missing_%26_Exploited_Children" title="International Centre for Missing &amp; Exploited Children">International Centre for Missing &amp; Exploited Children</a> (ICMEC).</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_employers">Largest employers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
