href="/wiki/Giant-Landover" title="Giant-Landover">Giant Food</a></td>\n<td>250\xe2\x80\x93499</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_culture">Arts and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Arts and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A popular Christmastime attraction in Alexandria is the Scottish Christmas Walk, which was established in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-saintandrewsociety.org_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saintandrewsociety.org-51">[51]</a></sup> The event, which involves a parade through the center of Old Town Alexandria, celebrates the city\'s Scottish heritage, and is the centerpiece of a yearly holiday festival.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> It serves as a fundraiser for social services in Alexandria.<sup id="cite_ref-saintandrewsociety.org_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saintandrewsociety.org-51">[51]</a></sup> Other parades in Old Town celebrate <a href="/wiki/Saint_Patrick%27s_Day" title="Saint Patrick\'s Day">Saint Patrick\'s Day</a><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Washington%27s_Birthday" title="Washington\'s Birthday">birthday of George Washington</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Other annual events include the Red Cross Waterfront Festival in June, various ethnic heritage days at Tavern Square, and "First Night Alexandria" which presents many family-friendly entertainments on New Year\'s Eve.</p>\n<p>These parades and other official events are typically led by Alexandria\'s town crier, who, often dressed in elaborately, by a tradition dating to the 18th century, in a red coat, breeches, black boots and a tricorne hat, welcomes participants.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Town_Alexandria.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photo of many buildings. Many are several stories high with red brick facade. They are arranged along a major street which extends from the front of the photo straight toward the back. In front is a Metrorail station with train tracks extending from the left to the right." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Old_Town_Alexandria.jpg/220px-Old_Town_Alexandria.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Old_Town_Alexandria.jpg/330px-Old_Town_Alexandria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Old_Town_Alexandria.jpg/440px-Old_Town_Alexandria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Town_Alexandria.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nOld Town Alexandria in March 2003, as seen from the observation deck of the <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_Masonic_National_Memorial" title="George Washington Masonic National Memorial">George Washington Masonic National Memorial</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexandria_torpedo_factory.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Tall modern building with big windows. Benches are in front." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Alexandria_torpedo_factory.jpg/170px-Alexandria_torpedo_factory.jpg" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Alexandria_torpedo_factory.jpg/255px-Alexandria_torpedo_factory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Alexandria_torpedo_factory.jpg/340px-Alexandria_torpedo_factory.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2580" data-file-height="3345" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexandria_torpedo_factory.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nAlexandria Torpedo Factory (waterfront side)</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Landmarks within the city include the <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_Masonic_National_Memorial" title="George Washington Masonic National Memorial">George Washington Masonic National Memorial</a> (also known as the <a href="/wiki/Freemasonry" title="Freemasonry">Masonic</a> Temple) and Observation Deck, <a href="/wiki/Christ_Church,_Alexandria" class="mw-redirect" title="Christ Church, Alexandria">Christ Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gadsby%27s_Tavern" title="Gadsby\'s Tavern">Gadsby\'s Tavern</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Carlyle_House" class="mw-redirect" title="John Carlyle House">John Carlyle House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Little_Theatre_of_Alexandria" title="Little Theatre of Alexandria">Little Theatre of Alexandria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lee-Fendall_House" class="mw-redirect" title="Lee-Fendall House">Lee-Fendall House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexandria_City_Hall" title="Alexandria City Hall">Alexandria City Hall</a>, Market Square, the <a href="/wiki/Jones_Point_Light" title="Jones Point Light">Jones Point Light</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Boundary_Markers_of_the_Original_District_of_Columbia" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Boundary Markers of the Original District of Columbia">the south cornerstone of the original District of Columbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Lee" title="Robert E. Lee">Robert E. Lee</a>\'s boyhood home, the <a href="/wiki/Torpedo_Factory_Art_Center" title="Torpedo Factory Art Center">Torpedo Factory Art Center</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Theological_Seminary" title="Virginia Theological Seminary">Virginia Theological Seminary</a>. Other sites of historical interest in the city include Alexandria Black History Resource Center, Fort Ward Park and Museum, and the Alexandria Canal lock re-creation at Canal Office Center. Interesting sites with Alexandria addresses but outside of the city limits include <a href="/wiki/River_Farm" title="River Farm">River Farm</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Collingwood_Library_%26_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Collingwood Library &amp; Museum (page does not exist)">Collingwood Library &amp; Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_Spring_Gardens_Park" title="Green Spring Gardens Park">Green Spring Gardens Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huntley_Meadows_Park" title="Huntley Meadows Park">Huntley Meadows Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Historic_Huntley" class="mw-redirect" title="Historic Huntley">Historic Huntley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pope-Leighey_House" class="mw-redirect" title="Pope-Leighey House">Pope-Leighey House</a> (designed by <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lloyd_Wright" title="Frank Lloyd Wright">Frank Lloyd Wright</a>), <a href="/wiki/Woodlawn_Plantation" class="mw-redirect" title="Woodlawn Plantation">Woodlawn Plantation</a>, Washington\'s Grist Mill and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Vernon" title="Mount Vernon">Mount Vernon</a> Estate.</p>\n<p>In 1830, John Hollensbury\'s home in Alexandria was one of two homes directly bordering an <a href="/wiki/Alleyway" title="Alleyway">alleyway</a> that received a large amount of <a href="/wiki/Horse-drawn_vehicle" title="Horse-drawn vehicle">horse-drawn wagon</a> traffic and loiterers.<sup id="cite_ref-beloved_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beloved-56">[56]</a></sup> In order to prevent people from using the alleyway, Hollensbury constructed a 7 feet (2.1&#160;m) wide, 25 feet (7.6&#160;m) deep, 325-square-foot (30.2&#160;m<sup>2</sup>), two story home using the existing brick walls of the adjacent homes for the sides of the new home.<sup id="cite_ref-beloved_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beloved-56">[56]</a></sup> The brick walls of the <a href="/wiki/Spite_house" title="Spite house">Hollensbury Spite House</a> living room have gouges from wagon-wheel hubs; the house is still standing, and is occupied.<sup id="cite_ref-beloved_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beloved-56">[56]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Due to its proximity to Washington, Alexandria has only been the home of one professional sports team, the <a href="/wiki/Alexandria_Dukes" title="Alexandria Dukes">Alexandria Dukes</a>, a minor league baseball team which has moved to <a href="/wiki/Woodbridge,_Virginia" title="Woodbridge, Virginia">Woodbridge</a> and is now named the <a href="/wiki/Potomac_Nationals" title="Potomac Nationals">Potomac Nationals</a>. However, the <a href="/wiki/Cal_Ripken_Collegiate_Baseball_League" title="Cal Ripken Collegiate Baseball League">Cal Ripken Collegiate Baseball League</a> brought baseball back to Alexandria in 2008 in the form of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria_(VA)_Aces&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alexandria (VA) Aces (page does not exist)">Alexandria Aces</a>. In addition, TC Williams, Bishop Ireton, St. Stephen\'s and Episcopal have storied histories in athletics, such as football, basketball, baseball and lacrosse. The largest youth sport in Alexandria is soccer with almost 2,500 players ages 2\xe2\x80\x9318 who participate in the Alexandria Soccer Association.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_recreation">Parks and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Parks and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Alexandria has a distributed park system with approximately 950 acres (3.8&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) spread across 70 major parks and 30 <a href="/wiki/Recreation" title="Recreation">recreation</a> centers, of which <a href="/wiki/Castanea_pumila" title="Castanea pumila">Chinquapin</a> is one of the largest. Chinquapin offers facilities for swimming, tennis, racquetball, and other sports. The city also organizes several sports leagues throughout the year including volleyball, softball and basketball.</p>\n<p>The city is home to <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Run_Regional_Park" title="Cameron Run Regional Park">Cameron Run Regional Park</a> which includes a water park with a <a href="/wiki/Wave_pool" title="Wave pool">wave pool</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_slide" title="Water slide">water slides</a>, as well as a <a href="/wiki/Miniature_golf" title="Miniature golf">miniature golf</a> course and batting cages. A portion of the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Vernon_Trail" title="Mount Vernon Trail">Mount Vernon Trail</a>, a popular bike and jogging path, runs through Old Town near the Potomac River on its way from the Mount Vernon Estate to Roosevelt Island in Washington, DC. There is also a largely unbroken line of parks stretching along the Alexandria waterfront from end to end.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexandria_(VA)_City_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Alexandria_%28VA%29_City_Hall.jpg/220px-Alexandria_%28VA%29_City_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Alexandria_%28VA%29_City_Hall.jpg/330px-Alexandria_%28VA%29_City_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Alexandria_%28VA%29_City_Hall.jpg/440px-Alexandria_%28VA%29_City_Hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexandria_(VA)_City_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nAlexandria City Hall</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<table align="center" border="2" cellpadding="4" cellspacing="0" style="float:right; background:honeyDew;">1.7% <i>41</i></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b><a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Virginia,_1916" title="United States presidential election in Virginia, 1916">1916</a></b></td>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6">25.8% <i>364</i></td>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b>73.5%</b> <i>1,038</i></td>\n<td style="text-align:center; background:honeyDew;">0.7% <i>10</i></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b><a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Virginia,_1912" title="United States presidential election in Virginia, 1912">1912</a></b></td>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6">11.0% <i>132</i></td>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b>79.2%</b> <i>951</i></td>\n<td style="text-align:center; background:honeyDew;">9.8% <i>118</i></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>As an independent city of Virginia (as opposed to an incorporated town within a county), Alexandria derives its governing authority from the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_General_Assembly" title="Virginia General Assembly">Virginia General Assembly</a>. In order to revise the power and structure of the city government, the city must request the General Assembly to amend the charter. The present charter was granted in 1950 and it has been amended in 1968, 1971, 1976, and 1982.</p>\n<p>Alexandria adopted a <a href="/wiki/Council-manager" class="mw-redirect" title="Council-manager">council-manager</a> form of government by way of referendum in 1921. This type of government empowers the elected City Council to pass legislation and appoint the City Manager. The City Manager is responsible for overseeing the city\'s administration.</p>\n<p>The Mayor, who is chosen on a separate ballot, presides over meetings of the Council and serves as the ceremonial head of government. The Mayor does not have the power to veto Council action. Council members traditionally choose the person receiving the most votes in the election to serve as Vice Mayor. In the absence or disability of the Mayor, the Vice Mayor performs the mayoral duties.</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>City Council<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></caption>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center; vertical-align:bottom;">Position</th>\n<th style="text-align:center;">Name</th>\n<th valign="bottom">Party</th>\n<th style="vertical-align:bottom; text-align:center;">First Election</th>\n<th style="vertical-align:bottom; text-align:center;">District</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#3333FF">&#160;</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/List_of_Mayors_of_Alexandria,_Virginia" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Mayors of Alexandria, Virginia">Mayor</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Allison_Silberberg" title="Allison Silberberg">Allison Silberberg</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2012</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/At-Large" class="mw-redirect" title="At-Large">At-Large</a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#3333FF">&#160;</td>\n<td>Vice Mayor</td>\n<td><a href="/w/index.php?title=Justin_Wilson_(local_politician)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Justin Wilson (local politician) (page does not exist)">Justin Wilson</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2007\xe2\x80\x932009<br />\n2012</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">At-Large</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#3333FF">&#160;</td>\n<td>Member</td>\n<td><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_T._Chapman&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="John T. Smedberg</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2003</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">At-Large</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#3333FF">&#160;</td>\n<td>Member</td>\n<td><a href="/w/index.php?title=Willie_Bailey_(Virginia_Politician)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Willie Bailey (Virginia Politician) (page does not exist)">Willie Bailey</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2015</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">At-Large</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>In 2008, the City of Alexandria had 78 standing local boards, commissions, and committees to advise the City Council on major issues affecting the community.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> All members are appointed by the City Council.</p>\n<p>Alexandria is part of <a href="/wiki/Virginia%27s_8th_congressional_district" title="Virginia\'s 8th congressional district">Virginia\'s 8th congressional district</a>, represented by Democrat and Alexandria resident <a href="/wiki/Don_Beyer" title="Don Beyer">Don Beyer</a>, elected in 2014.</p>\n<p>The state\'s senior member of the United States Senate is Democrat <a href="/wiki/Mark_Warner" title="Mark Warner">Mark Warner</a>, elected in 2008. The state\'s junior member of the United States Senate is Democrat <a href="/wiki/Tim_Kaine" title="Tim Kaine">Tim Kaine</a>, elected in 2012.</p>\n<p>The city operates a jail for pre-trial and short-term inmates. This jail is used to house pre-trial inmates in federal espionage cases.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecocity">Ecocity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ecocity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2008 the city council approved a charter where "citizens, businesses, and city government participate in a vibrant community that is always mindful of the needs and lifestyles of the generations to come."<sup id="cite_ref-Eco-City_Charter_2008_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eco-City_Charter_2008-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:4</sup> That chater defined sustainability as "meeting our community\xe2\x80\x99s present needs while preserving our historic character and ensuring the ability of future generations to meet their own needs."<sup id="cite_ref-Eco-City_Charter_2008_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eco-City_Charter_2008-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:5</sup> In <i>Ecocity Berkeley</i> Register defined an ecocity as "an ecologically healthy city."<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:3</sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NVCC_-_Alexandria_campus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Big street with cars waiting at intersection" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/NVCC_-_Alexandria_campus.jpg/220px-NVCC_-_Alexandria_campus.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/NVCC_-_Alexandria_campus.jpg/330px-NVCC_-_Alexandria_campus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/NVCC_-_Alexandria_campus.jpg/440px-NVCC_-_Alexandria_campus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NVCC_-_Alexandria_campus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nEntrance to <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia_Community_College" title="Northern Virginia Community College">Northern Virginia Community College</a>\'s Alexandria campus</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The city is served by the <a href="/wiki/Alexandria_City_Public_Schools" title="Alexandria City Public Schools">Alexandria City Public Schools</a> system and by the Alexandria campus of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia_Community_College" title="Northern Virginia Community College">Northern Virginia Community College</a>. The largest seminary in the <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_in_the_United_States_of_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Episcopal Church in the United States of America">Episcopal Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Theological_Seminary" title="Virginia Theological Seminary">Virginia Theological Seminary</a>, is located on Seminary Road. <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Polytechnic_Institute_and_State_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Virginia Polytechnic Institute and State University">Virginia Tech\'s</a> Washington-Alexandria Architecture Center, also known as WAAC, is located on Prince Street in Old Town, offering graduate programs in Urban Affairs and Planning, Public and International Affairs, Architecture, and Landscape Architecture. <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Commonwealth_University" title="Virginia Commonwealth University">Virginia Commonwealth University</a> operates a Northern Virginia branch of its School of Social Work and <a href="/wiki/The_George_Washington_University" class="mw-redirect" title="The George Washington University">The George Washington University</a> (Washington DC) also has a campus near the King Street metro. This campus mainly offers professional and vocational programs, such as an executive MBA program, urban planning and security studies.</p>\n<p>Alexandria has several of the Washington, D.C., area\'s top private schools, such as <a href="/wiki/St._Stephen%27s_and_St._Agnes_School" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Stephen\'s and St. Agnes School">St. Stephen\'s and St. Agnes School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bishop_Ireton_High_School" title="Bishop Ireton High School">Bishop Ireton High School</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_High_School_(Alexandria,_Virginia)" title="Episcopal High School (Alexandria, Virginia)">Episcopal High School</a>. Also in the city are Alexandria Country Day School, Commonwealth Academy, St. Mary\'s Catholic School, St. Rita\'s Catholic School, Blessed Sacrament School and <a href="/wiki/Global_Health_College" title="Global Health College">Global Health College</a>.</p>\n<p>Alexandria\'s public school system consists of thirteen elementary schools for grades 5-year-old Kindergarten through Grade 5. Middle Schools, George Washington and Francis C. Hammond, serve 6th through 8th graders. Minnie Howard Ninth Grade Center and <a href="/wiki/T.C._Williams_High_School" class="mw-redirect" title="T.C. Williams High School">T.C. Williams High School</a> serve grades 9th and 10 through 12, respectively, for the entire city.</p>\n<p>The demographics of Alexandria City Public Schools contrast with those of the city. In 2008, only 14% of the students at Francis C. Hammond Middle School were non-Hispanic whites, compared to about 60% when looking at the city as a whole. 27% were of Hispanic descent, and 48% were black. About 9% of the school was of Asian descent. In 2004, 62% of the schoolgoing children received free lunches; by 2008, that number had decreased to 56%.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> At George Washington Middle School, 30% of students are non-Hispanic whites, 24% were Hispanic, and 41% was black; 3% of the students were Asian, and 52% of students received free lunch.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> T.C. Williams High School follows this trend as well; 23% of the students were classified as non-Hispanic whites, 25% as Hispanic, and 44% as black. 7% of the school was Asian, and 47% of all students received free lunch.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amtrak_82_at_Alexandria_Union_Station_in_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Big shiny train facing us, at station with passengers on platform" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Amtrak_82_at_Alexandria_Union_Station_in_2007.jpg/220px-Amtrak_82_at_Alexandria_Union_Station_in_2007.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Amtrak_82_at_Alexandria_Union_Station_in_2007.jpg/330px-Amtrak_82_at_Alexandria_Union_Station_in_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Amtrak_82_at_Alexandria_Union_Station_in_2007.jpg/440px-Amtrak_82_at_Alexandria_Union_Station_in_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3502" data-file-height="2308" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amtrak_82_at_Alexandria_Union_Station_in_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nSouthbound <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> train at Alexandria\'s Union Station</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Alexandria is bisected east and west by <a href="/wiki/State_Route_7_(Virginia)" class="mw-redirect" title="State Route 7 (Virginia)">State Route 7</a>, known as <a href="/wiki/King_Street,_Alexandria,_Virginia" class="mw-redirect" title="King Street, Alexandria, Virginia">King Street</a>. The most western section of King St here once was the terminus of the Leesburg Turnpike. Interstate 95/495 (the <a href="/wiki/Interstate_495_(Capital_Beltway)" title="Interstate 495 (Capital Beltway)">Capital Beltway</a>), including the <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson_Bridge" title="Woodrow Wilson Bridge">Woodrow Wilson Bridge</a> over the Potomac River, approximately parallels the city\'s southern boundary with Fairfax County. <a href="/wiki/Interstate_395_(District_of_Columbia-Virginia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Interstate 395 (District of Columbia-Virginia)">Interstate 395</a> crosses north and south through the western part of the city. Other major routes include north\xe2\x80\x93south <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_Virginia" title="U.S. Route 1 in Virginia">U.S. 1</a> (Patrick and Henry Streets after <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Henry" title="Patrick Henry">Patrick Henry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Davis_Highway#Virginia" title="Jefferson Davis Highway">Jefferson Davis Highway</a> and Richmond Highway), Washington St/<a href="/wiki/George_Washington_Memorial_Parkway" title="George Washington Memorial Parkway">George Washington Memorial Parkway</a>, Russell Rd, Quaker Lane, Van Dorn St and Beauregard St, and east\xe2\x80\x93west Duke Street (<a href="/wiki/State_Route_236_(Virginia)" class="mw-redirect" title="State Route 236 (Virginia)">State Route 236</a>), Braddock Rd and Janneys Lane/Seminary Rd.</p>\n<p>Alexandria is south of, adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan_Washington_National_Airport" title="Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport">Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport</a> in Arlington County. Alexandria is also near to <a href="/wiki/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport" title="Washington Dulles International Airport">Washington Dulles International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dulles,_Virginia" title="Dulles, Virginia">Dulles, Virginia</a>.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Alexandria)" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Station (Alexandria)">Alexandria Union Station</a>, the city\'s historic train station, has <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> intercity services and the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Railway_Express" title="Virginia Railway Express">Virginia Railway Express</a> regional rail service. The station is directly adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/King_Street_%E2%80%93_Old_Town_(WMATA_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="King Street \xe2\x80\x93 Old Town (WMATA station)">King Street \xe2\x80\x93 Old Town</a> <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metro" title="Washington Metro">Washington Metro</a> station, at the convergence of the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Line_(Washington_Metro)" title="Blue Line (Washington Metro)">Blue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Line_(Washington_Metro)" title="Yellow Line (Washington Metro)">Yellow Lines</a>. Three other Metro stations in Alexandria are <a href="/wiki/Braddock_Road_(Washington_Metro)" class="mw-redirect" title="Braddock Road (Washington Metro)">Braddock Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Van_Dorn_Street_(Washington_Metro)" class="mw-redirect" title="Van Dorn Street (Washington Metro)">Van Dorn Street</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eisenhower_Avenue_(Washington_Metro)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eisenhower Avenue (Washington Metro)">Eisenhower Avenue</a>.</p>\n<p>The traditional boundary between Old Town and the latterly annexed sections of the city followed the railway now owned by <a href="/wiki/CSX_Transportation" title="CSX Transportation">CSX Transportation</a>.</p>\n<p>The city government operates its own mass transit system, the <a href="/wiki/DASH_(bus)" title="DASH (bus)">DASH</a> bus, connecting points of interest with local transit hubs. <a href="/wiki/Metrobus_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Metrobus (Washington, D.C.)">Metrobus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metro" title="Washington Metro">Washington Metro</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Railway_Express" title="Virginia Railway Express">Virginia Railway Express</a>, better known as the VRE, also serve Alexandria. The city also offers a free "trolley" diesel bus service on King Street from the King Street Metro Station to the Waterfront<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> and a water taxi to and from the <a href="/wiki/National_Harbor" class="mw-redirect" title="National Harbor">National Harbor</a> development in Prince George\'s County, Maryland.</p>\n<p>Until 2014, local legislation mandated that all new north/south streets in the city be named for Confederate military leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-WBJ_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WBJ-67">[67]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_libraries">Public libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Public libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px">\n<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n<div class="thumbimage"><a 2x" data-file-width="6144" data-file-height="4096" /></a></div>\n</div>\n<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n<div class="thumbimage"><a 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Beatley_Central_Library%2C_Alexandria%2C_Virginia_LCCN2012630097.tif/lossy-page1-400px-Beatley_Central_Library%2C_Alexandria%2C_Virginia_LCCN2012630097.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6144" data-file-height="4096" /></a></div>\n</div>\n<div style="clear:left"></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Reading rooms within city libraries</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Alexandria_Library,_Virginia" title="Alexandria Library, Virginia">Alexandria Library</a> serves the residents of the City of Alexandria with four locations:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_E._Beatley,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Charles E. Beatley, Jr.">Charles E. Beatley, Jr.</a> Central Library (Main branch): 5005 Duke Street, Alexandria</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kate_Waller_Barrett" title="Kate Waller Barrett">Kate Waller Barrett</a> Branch: 717 Queen Street, Alexandria</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ellen_Coolidge_Burke" title="Ellen Coolidge Burke">Ellen Coolidge Burke</a> Branch: 4701 Seminary Road, Alexandria</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_M._Duncan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="James M. Duncan (page does not exist)">James M. Duncan</a> Branch: 2501 Commonwealth Avenue, Alexandria</li>\n</ul>\n<p>The library system provides a variety of services which include adult, young adult, and children\'s materials, as well as access to genealogy records and full text articles from thousands of magazines and newspapers through online databases. E-Books can be borrowed through <a href="/wiki/OverDrive,_Inc." title="OverDrive, Inc.">OverDrive</a> e-Audio books and all branches offer free public Internet access and free Wifi.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Alexandria Library maintains a reciprocal agreement with neighboring libraries in Arlington, District of Columbia, Fairfax, Falls Church, Fauquier, Frederick, Loudoun, Montgomery, Prince George\'s, and Prince William.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-3" style="-moz-column-count: 3; -webkit-column-count: 3; column-count: 3;">\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cass_Elliot" title="Cass Elliot">Cass Elliot</a> and John Phillips of <a href="/wiki/The_Mamas_%26_The_Papas" class="mw-redirect" title="The Mamas &amp; The Papas">The Mamas &amp; The Papas</a><sup id="cite_ref-visitalexandriava_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitalexandriava-27">[27]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Chad_Dukes_(radio_personality)" title="Chad Dukes (radio personality)">Chad Dukes</a>, Alexandria, Virginia radio personality, pioneer in podcasting<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dean_Muhtadi" class="mw-redirect" title="Dean Muhtadi">Dean Muhtadi</a>, former <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> player and current <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">WWE</a> wrestler<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Diedrich_Bader" title="Diedrich Bader">Diedrich Bader</a>, actor<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eddie_Royal" title="Eddie Royal">Eddie Royal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Chicago Bears</a> wide receiver<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gerald_R._Ford" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerald R. Ford">Gerald R. Ford</a>, former President of the United States, lived in <a href="/wiki/Parkfairfax,_Virginia" title="Parkfairfax, Virginia">Parkfairfax</a>, and later on Crown View Drive<sup id="cite_ref-Parkfairfax_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parkfairfax-74">[74]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Thad_Levine" title="Thad Levine">Thad Levine</a>, general manager of <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Minnesota Twins</a>, was born in Alexandria</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jim_Morrison" title="Jim Morrison">Jim Morrison</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Doors" title="The Doors">The Doors</a><sup id="cite_ref-visitalexandriava_27-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitalexandriava-27">[27]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Megan_Young" title="Megan Young">Megan Young</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miss_World_Philippines_2013" title="Miss World Philippines 2013">Miss World Philippines 2013</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miss_World_2013" title="Miss World 2013">Miss World 2013</a><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_M._Nixon" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard M. Nixon">Richard M. Nixon</a>, former President of the United States, lived in <a href="/wiki/Parkfairfax" class="mw-redirect" title="Parkfairfax">Parkfairfax</a><sup id="cite_ref-Parkfairfax_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parkfairfax-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:11</sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rick_Franklin" title="Rick Franklin">Rick Franklin</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_blues" title="Piedmont blues">Piedmont blues</a> guitarist, singer and songwriter, was born in Alexandria.<sup id="cite_ref-Eagle_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eagle-76">[76]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Lee" title="Robert E. href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Willard_Scott" title="Willard Scott">Willard Scott</a>, national television personality, grew up in Rosemont<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandria,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image">\n<div style="width:52px"><img alt="" War</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Walking_Dead_(comic_book)" title="The Walking Dead (comic book)">The Walking Dead</a></i> comic book series and subsequent <a href="/wiki/The_Walking_Dead_(TV_series)" title="The Walking Dead (TV series)">TV adaptation</a> features a protected area of Alexandria known as the <a href="/wiki/Alexandria_Safe-Zone" href="/wiki/Remember_the_Titans" title="Remember the Titans">Remember the Titans</a></i> takes place in Alexandria and the cemetery scene was filmed at <a href="/wiki/Ivy_Hill_Cemetery_(Alexandria,_Virginia)" title="Ivy Hill Cemetery (Alexandria, Virginia)">Ivy Hill Cemetery</a> in Alexandria.</li>\n<li>Alternative rock band the <a href="/wiki/Foo_Fighters" title="Foo Fighters">Foo Fighters</a> has a track titled "<a href="/wiki/Arlandria_(Foo_Fighters_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Arlandria (Foo Fighters song)">Arlandria</a>" on their 2011 release <i><a href="/wiki/Wasting_Light" title="Wasting Light">Wasting Light</a></i>; front man (and ex-<a href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)" title="Nirvana (band)">Nirvana</a> drummer) <a href="/wiki/Dave_Grohl" title="Dave Grohl">Dave Grohl</a> lived in Alexandria during his childhood. The Arlandria neighborhood is also referenced in the song "Headwires" from the band\'s 1999 release, <i><a href="/wiki/There_Is_Nothing_Left_to_Lose" title="There Is Nothing Left to Lose">There Is Nothing Left to Lose</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></li>\n<li>In <i><a href="/wiki/The_X-Files" title="The X-Files">The X-Files</a></i>, the href="/wiki/County-equivalent" class="mw-redirect" title="County-equivalent">county equivalents</a>. Virginia\'s incorporated cities are listed under their surrounding county. The incorporated cities bordering more than one county (<a class="mw-selflink selflink">Alexandria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falls_Church,_Virginia" title="Falls Church, Virginia">Falls Church</a> and <a
